These will also become red flags if the implementation changes.",

    "title": "Change shipping rates cache",
    "user": {

      "avatar_url": "https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/212829?v=3",

      "starred_url": "https://api.github.com/users/ekosz/starred{/owner}{/repo}",
      "subscriptions_url": "https://api.github.com/users/ekosz/subscriptions",
      "organizations_url": "https://api.github.com/users/ekosz/orgs",

      "site_admin": false
    },
    "body": "### Problem \r\n\r\nWe need to update domestic shipping rates on the site from $3.85 + $1.00 to $3.99 + $2.00. The current shipping rates cache made makes this a very difficult to change. The problem right now is that when we update the rates, the current cache won't expire for 24 hours. Thats 24 hours where users will see $3.85 on checkout, but charged $3.99 when they finish.\r\n\r\n### Solution\r\n\r\nRemove the public `Cache-Control`, and replace it with a public `Etag` that is very fast to verify. The new flow looks like this.\r\n\r\n1. The very first time a shipping rate is requested for a campaign:\r\n  1. It finds the rate\r\n  1. Generates an `Etag` composed of the campaign's region and the most recent shipping rate `updated_at`\r\n  1. Returns the rates\r\n1. Every other request to the shipping rates will:\r\n  1. Check if the campaign's region or most recent shipping rate changed\r\n  1. If NOT return the old rates (without spending time looking them up)\r\n  1. If SO Repeat step 1\r\n\r\nThis keeps the request still very fast and cached (only performing 3 SQL calls), but invalidates itself when the rates update.  This is a good example where we create a compromise between speed and dymacy.\r\n\r\n### QA Instructions\r\n\r\n1. Visit a checkout page and note the shipping rate\r\n1. Refresh the page, you should see the same shipping rate\r\n1. Ask Eric to update the shipping rates for staging\r\n1. Refresh the page, you should see the new shipping rate\r\n1. Finish checkout, you should have been charged the new shipping rate",

    "body": "### Problem\r\n\r\nWe are using an outdated method for loading assets over a protocol relative url. I originally got this idea from Paul Irish's blog http://www.paulirish.com/2010/the-protocol-relative-url/. But if you look at the blog post now he's updated it to say:\r\n\r\n> Now that SSL is encouraged for everyone and doesn’t have performance concerns, this technique is now an anti-pattern. If the asset you need is available on SSL, then always use the https:// asset.\r\n\r\n> Allowing the snippet to request over HTTP opens the door for attacks like the recent Github Man-on-the-side attack. It’s always safe to request HTTPS assets even if your site is on HTTP, however the reverse is not true.\r\n\r\n> More guidance and details in Eric Mills’ guide to CDNs & HTTPS.\r\n\r\n\r\n### Solution\r\n\r\nStop using `//` for all of our urls, and strictly load assets over `https://`.\r\n\r\n### QA Instructions\r\n\r\n1. Smoke test the entire site :(\r\n1. Make sure all of the assets are loading properly",

    "body": "#### Problem\r\nErrors are being thrown in the `DesignPathedSVGGeneratorWorker` & the\r\n`AbsoluteDesignPathedSVGGeneratorWorker` relating to designs coming\r\nthrough and not having a campaign associated with them\r\n\r\n#### Solution\r\nThe code change remediates the process through which the designs can\r\nbecome corrupted\r\n\r\n#### Recreating\r\n* Create a New Active Campaign (It needs a user, and an active campaign state)\r\n* In the rails console find the id for the design of the campaign\r\n\r\n  ```bash\r\n    $ rails c\r\n  ```\r\n  ```ruby\r\n    [1] pry(main)> campaign = Campaign.find_by_name($CAMPAIGN_NAME)\r\n  #=> #<Campaign id: 1, additional_images: nil, address: \"\",.... zip: \"\">\r\n    [2] pry(main)> design = campaign.design\r\n  #=> #<Design id: 1, bypass_vectorization: false,... version: 0>\r\n    [3] pry(main)> design.id\r\n  #=> 1\r\n  ```\r\n\r\n* In the admin interface find the Campaign & start a Revision\r\n* Redesign the campaign and safe it\r\n* In the admin interface find the Campaign & select the Push Live button\r\n* In the rails console execute the workers for the original design\r\n\r\n* __BEFORE FIX__\r\n\r\n  ```bash\r\n    $ rails c\r\n  ```\r\n  ```ruby\r\n    [1] pry(main)> Seller::AbsoluteDesignPathedSVGGeneratorWorker.new.perform(1)\r\n  #   Design Load (0.4ms)  SELECT  `designs`.* FROM `designs`  WHERE `designs`.`id` = 1 LIMIT 1\r\n  # RuntimeError: Design lacks a campaign\r\n  # from /www/rails-teespring/apps/seller/app/workers/seller/absolute_design_pathed_svg_generator_worker.rb:9:in `perform'`\r\n    [2] pry(main)> Seller::DesignPathedSVGGeneratorWorker.new.perform(1)\r\n  #   Design Load (0.4ms)  SELECT  `designs`.* FROM `designs`  WHERE `designs`.`id` = 1 LIMIT 1\r\n  # RuntimeError: Design lacks a campaign\r\n  # from /www/rails-teespring/apps/seller/app/workers/seller/design_pathed_svg_generator_worker.rb:9:in `perform'`\r\n  ```\r\n\r\n* __AFTER FIX__ (REPEAT WHOLE PROCCESS)\r\n\r\n  ```ruby\r\n    [1] pry(main)> Seller::DesignPathedSVGGeneratorWorker.new.perform(2)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  [3/824]\r\n  # Design Load (1.1ms)  SELECT  `designs`.* FROM `designs`  WHERE `designs`.`id` = 2 LIMIT 1\r\n  # Campaign Load (0.5ms)  SELECT  `campaigns`.* FROM `campaigns`  WHERE `campaigns`.`id` = 1 LIMIT 1\r\n  # Design Load (0.3ms)  SELECT `designs`.* FROM `designs`  WHERE `designs`.`state` IN (0, 1) AND `designs`.`campaign_id` IN (1)  ORDER BY `designs`.`version` DESC\r\n  # DesignAsset Load (0.3ms)  SELECT  `design_assets`.* FROM `design_assets`  WHERE `design_assets`.`design_id` = 2 AND `design_assets`.`side` = 'FRONT'  ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT 1\r\n  # Product Load (0.3ms)  SELECT  `products`.* FROM `products`  WHERE `products`.`id` = 222 LIMIT 1\r\n  # PaperTrail::Version Load (0.4ms)  SELECT  `versions`.* FROM `versions`  WHERE `versions`.`item_id` = 222 AND `versions`.`item_type` = 'Product' AND (`versions`.`created_at` > '2015-04-26 20:41:52')  ORDER BY `versions`.`created_at` ASC, `versions`.`id` ASC LIMIT 1\r\n  # ...\r\n  ```\r\n",

    "body": "### Problem\r\n\r\nThere is currently no programmatic way to tell if a user is looking at a campaign page solely via its url. It could be an about page, a targeted landing page, etc.\r\n\r\n### Solution\r\n\r\nPrefix all campaign (and campaign-like) urls with `/c/`. In this scheme `teespring.com/cloudyrochester` would become `teespring.com/c/cloudyrochester`. That way we can easily tell if someone is looking at campaign page. This allows a lot more edge side logic outside of our application servers.\r\n\r\nThis PR also adds a fallback for the old urls to be redirected to the new url scheme.\r\n\r\n### Caveats \r\n\r\n1. Localization prefixes will still come before the `/c/`. So `teespring.com/fr/cloudyrochester` -> `teespring.com/fr/c/cloudyrochester`\r\n1. The redirects from the old scheme to new scheme is currently a 301 redirect. Which means rolling this back could be detrimental.\r\n\r\nLets use this PR as a place to discuss this change. ping @kadira @goodgravy to start",

Besides tracking the order itself, we are also going to be tracking each of its line items as separate events.\r\n\r\n@rrzein @jonny5 @stephenchen13 Can you take a look please?\r\n\r\n**QA instructions**:\r\n\r\n* You should be able to cancel orders without any trouble\r\n* Please test the following 4 ways of canceling orders, and check for both ``orders.canceled`` and ``item.canceled`` in each scenario:\r\n\r\n1) Purchase an item, then cancel it via your purchase confirmation email\r\n\r\n2) Login as an admin and cancel a placed order\r\n\r\n3) Fail a campaign (orders placed < min to print orders)\r\n\r\n4) Buy a campaign with a fake, incomplete address. Then end the campaign (orders placed >= min to print orders)\r\n\r\nParameters for ``order.canceled`` should include:\r\n+        campaign_root_id\r\n+        campaign_id\r\n+        order_id\r\n+        quantity\r\n+        reason\r\n+        cancelled_at\r\n\r\nParameters for ``item.canceled`` should include:\r\n+        product_id\r\n+        color_id\r\n+        quantity\r\n+        order_id\r\n+        campaign_id\r\n+        campaign_root_id",
